\\tsched.SchedulingQueue.Run(logger)\\n438: \\n439: \\t// We need to start scheduleOne loop in a dedicated goroutine,\\n440: \\t// because scheduleOne function hangs on getting the next item\\n441: \\t// from the SchedulingQueue.\\n442: \\t// If there are no new pods to schedule, it will be hanging there\\n443: \\t// and if done in this goroutine it will be blocking closing\\n444: \\t// Nodes,\\n862: // and the top of the list will be always the selected host.\\n863: func selectHost(nodeScoreList []framework.NodePluginScores, count int) (string, []framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\\n864: \\tif len(nodeScoreList) == 0 {\\n865: \\t\\treturn \\\"\\\", nil, errEmptyPriorityList\\n866: \\t}\\n867: \\n868: \\tvar h nodeScoreHeap = nodeScoreList\\n869: \\theap.Init(&h)\\n870: scores get checked for a reservoir sampling,\\n877: \\t// and sortedNodeScoreList gets (count - 1) elements.\\n878: \\tfor ns := heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores); ; ns = node list.\n388: // If it succeeds, it will return the name of the node.\n389: // If it fails, it will return a FitError with reasons.\n390: func (sched *Scheduler) schedulePod(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) (result ScheduleResult, err error) {\n391: \ttrace := utiltrace.New(\"Scheduling\", utiltrace.Field{Key: \"namespace\", Value: pod.Namespace}, utiltrace.Field{Key: \"name\", Value: pod.Name})\n392: \tdefer trace.LogIfLong(100 * time.Millisecond)\n393: \tif err := sched.Cache.UpdateSnapshot(klog.FromContext(ctx), sched.nodeInfoSnapshot); err != nil {\n394: \t\treturn result, err\n395: \t}\n396: \ttrace.Step(\"Snapshotting scheduler cache and node infos done\")\n397: \n398: \tif \tif err != nil {\n404: \t\treturn result, err\n405: \t}\n406: \ttrace.Step(\"Computing predicates done\")\n407: \n408: \tif len(feasibleNodes) == 0 {\n409: \t\treturn result, \t\tFeasibleNodes:  len(feasibleNodes),\n437: \t}, err\n438: }\n439: \n440: // Filters the nodes to find the ones that fit the pod based on the framework\n441: // filter plugins and filter extenders.\n442: func (sched *Scheduler) findNodesThatFitPod(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, framework.Diagnosis, error) {\n443: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n444: \tdiagnosis := framework.Diagnosis{\n445: \t\tNodeToStatusMap: make(framework.NodeToStatusMap),\n446: \t}\n447: \n448: \tallNodes, err := sched.nodeInfoSnapshot.NodeInfos().List()\n449: \tif err != nil {\n450: \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, err\n451: \t}\n452: \t// Run \"prefilter\" plugins.\n453: \tpreRes, s := fwk.RunPreFilterPlugins(ctx, \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, nil\n470: \t}\n471: \n472: \t// \"NominatedNodeName\" can potentially be set in a previous scheduling cycle as a result of preemption.\n473: \t// This node is likely the only candidate that will fit the pod, and hence we try it first before iterating over all nodes.\n474: \tif len(pod.Status.NominatedNodeName) > 0 {\n475: \t\tfeasibleNodes, err := sched.evaluateNominatedNode(ctx, pod, fwk, state, diagnosis)\n476: \t\tif err != nil {\n477: \t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Evaluation failed on nominated node\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"node\", pod.Status.NominatedNodeName)\n478: \t\t}\n479: \t\t// Nominated node passes all the filters, scheduler is good to assign this node to the pod.\n480: \t\tif len(feasibleNodes) != 0 {\n481: \t\t\treturn feasibleNodes, diagnosis, nil\n482: \t\t}\n483: \t}\n484: \n485: \tnodes := allNodes\n486: \tif !preRes.AllNodes() {\n487: \t\tnodes = make([]*framework.NodeInfo, 0, len(preRes.NodeNames))\n488: \t\tfor _, n := range allNodes {\n489: \t\t\tif !preRes.NodeNames.Has(n.Node().Name) {\n490: \t\t\t\t// We consider Nodes that are filtered out by PreFilterResult as \t\t\t}\n495: \t\t\tnodes = append(nodes, n)\n496: \t\t}\n497: \t}\n498: \tfeasibleNodes, err := sched.findNodesThatPassFilters(ctx, fwk, state, pod, &diagnosis, nodes)\n499: \t// always try to update the sched.nextStartNodeIndex regardless of whether an error has occurred\n500: \t// this is helpful to make sure that all the nodes have a chance to be searched\n501: \tprocessedNodes := len(feasibleNodes) + len(diagnosis.NodeToStatusMap)\n502: \tsched.nextStartNodeIndex = (sched.nextStartNodeIndex + processedNodes) % len(nodes)\n503: \tif err != nil {\n504: \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, kind of requeueing feature like EnqueueExtensions in the scheduling framework.\n515: \t\t// When Extenders reject some Nodes and the pod ends up being unschedulable,\n516: \t\t// we put framework.ExtenderName to pInfo.UnschedulablePlugins.\n517: \t\t// This Pod will be requeued from unschedulable pod pool to activeQ/backoffQ\n518: \t\t// by any kind of cluster events.\n519: \t\t// https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/122019\n520: \t\tif diagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins == nil {\n521: \t\t\tdiagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins = sets.New[string]()\n522: \t\t}\n523: \t\tdiagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins.Insert(framework.ExtenderName)\n524: \t}\n525: \n526: \treturn feasibleNodesAfterExtender, diagnosis, nil\n527: }\n528: \n529: func (sched *Scheduler) \n562: // hasExtenderFilters checks if any extenders filter nodes.\n563: func (sched *Scheduler) hasExtenderFilters() bool {\n564: \tfor _, extender := range sched.Extenders {\n565: \t\tif *Scheduler) findNodesThatPassFilters(\n574: \tctx context.Context,\n575: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n576: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n577: \tpod *v1.Pod,\n578: \tdiagnosis *framework.Diagnosis,\n579: \tnodes []*framework.NodeInfo) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, error) {\n580: \tnumAllNodes := len(nodes)\n581: \tnumNodesToFind := sched.numFeasibleNodesToFind(fwk.PercentageOfNodesToScore(), int32(numAllNodes))\n582: \tif !sched.hasExtenderFilters() && !sched.hasScoring(fwk) {\n583: \t\tnumNodesToFind = 1\n584: \t}\n585: \n586: \t// Create feasible list with enough space to avoid growing it\n587: \t// and allow assigning.\n588: \tfeasibleNodes := make([]*framework.NodeInfo, numNodesToFind)\n589: \n590: \tif \t}\n596: \n597: \terrCh := parallelize.NewErrorChannel()\n598: \tvar feasibleNodesLen int32\n599: \tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n600: \tdefer cancel()\n601: \n602: \ttype nodeStatus struct {\n603: \t\tnode   string\n604: \t\tstatus *framework.Status\n605: \t}\n606: \tresult := make([]*nodeStatus, numAllNodes)\n607: \tcheckNode := func(i int) {\n608: \t\t// We check the nodes starting from where we left off in the previous scheduling cycle,\n609: \t\t// this is to make sure all nodes have the same chance of being examined across pods.\n610: \t\tnodeInfo := nodes[(sched.nextStartNodeIndex+i)%numAllNodes]\n611: \t\tstatus := fwk.RunFilterPluginsWithNominatedPods(ctx, state, pod, nodeInfo)\n612: \t\tif status.Code() == framework.Error {\n613: \t\t\terrCh.SendErrorWithCancel(status.AsError(), cancel)\n614: \t\t\treturn\n615: \t\t}\n616: \t\tif status.IsSuccess() {\n617: \t\t\tlength := atomic.AddInt32(&feasibleNodesLen, 1)\n618: \t\t\tif length > numNodesToFind {\n619: \t\t\t\tcancel()\n620: \t\t\t\tatomic.AddInt32(&feasibleNodesLen, -1)\n621: \t\t\t} else {\n622: \t\t\t\tfeasibleNodes[length-1] = nodeInfo\n623: \t\t\t}\n624: \t\t} else {\n625: \t\t\tresult[i] = &nodeStatus{node: nodeInfo.Node().Name, status: status}\n626: \t\t}\n627: \t}\n628: \n629: \tbeginCheckNode := time.Now()\n630: \tstatusCode := framework.Success\n631: \tdefer func() {\n632: \t\t// We record Filter extension point latency here instead of in framework.go because framework.RunFilterPlugins\n633: \t\t// function is called for each node, whereas we want to have an overall latency for all nodes per scheduling cycle.\n634: \t\t// Note that this latency also includes latency for `addNominatedPods`, which calls framework.RunPreFilterAddPod.\n635: \t\tmetrics.FrameworkExtensionPointDuration.WithLabelValues(metrics.Filter, statusCode.String(), fwk.ProfileName()).Observe(metrics.SinceInSeconds(beginCheckNode))\n636: \t}()\n637: \n638: \t// Stops searching for more nodes once the configured number of feasible nodes\n639: \t// are found.\n640: \tfwk.Parallelizer().Until(ctx, numAllNodes, checkNode, metrics.Filter)\n641: \tfeasibleNodes = feasibleNodes[:feasibleNodesLen]\n642: \tfor _, item := range result {\n643: \t\tif item == nil {\n644: \t\t\tcontinue\n645: \t\t}\n646: \t\tdiagnosis.NodeToStatusMap[item.node] = item.status\n647: \t\tdiagnosis.AddPluginStatus(item.status)\n648: \t}\n649: \tif err := errCh.ReceiveError(); err != nil {\n650: \t\tstatusCode = framework.Error\n651: \t\treturn feasibleNodes, err\n652: \t}\n653: \treturn feasibleNodes, nil\n654: }\n655: \n656: // numFeasibleNodesToFind returns the number of feasible nodes that once found, the scheduler stops\n657: // its search for more feasible nodes.\n658: func (sched *Scheduler) numFeasibleNodesToFind(percentageOfNodesToScore *int32, numAllNodes int32) (numNodes int32) {\n659: \tif numAllNodes < minFeasibleNodesToFind {\n660: \t\treturn numAllNodes\n661: \t}\n662: \n663: \t// Use profile percentageOfNodesToScore if it's set. Otherwise, use global percentageOfNodesToScore.\n664: \tvar percentage int32\n665: \tif percentageOfNodesToScore != nil {\n666: \t\tpercentage = *percentageOfNodesToScore\n667: \t} else {\n668: \t\tpercentage = sched.percentageOfNodesToScore\n669: \t}\n670: \n671: \tif percentage == 0 {\n672: \t\tpercentage = int32(50) - numAllNodes/125\n673: \t\tif percentage < minFeasibleNodesPercentageToFind {\n674: \t\t\tpercentage = minFeasibleNodesPercentageToFind\n675: \t\t}\n676: \t}\n677: \n678: \tnumNodes = numAllNodes * percentage / 100\n679: \tif numNodes < minFeasibleNodesToFind {\n680: \t\treturn minFeasibleNodesToFind\n681: \t}\n682: \n683: \treturn numNodes\n684: }\n685: \n686: func findNodesThatPassExtenders(ctx context.Context, extenders []framework.Extender, pod *v1.Pod, feasibleNodes []*framework.NodeInfo, statuses framework.NodeToStatusMap) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, error) {\n687: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n688: \t// Extenders are called sequentially.\n689: \t// Nodes in original feasibleNodes can be excluded in one extender, and pass on to the next\n690: \t// extender in a decreasing manner.\n691: \tfor _, extender := range extenders {\n692: \t\tif len(feasibleNodes) == 0 {\n693: \t\t\tbreak\n694: \t\t}\n695: \t\tif !extender.IsInterested(pod) {\n696: \t\t\tcontinue\n697: \t\t}\n698: \n699: \t\t// Status of failed nodes in failedAndUnresolvableMap will be added or overwritten in <statuses>,\n700: \t\t// so that the scheduler framework can respect the UnschedulableAndUnresolvable status for\n701: \t\t// particular nodes, and this may eventually improve preemption efficiency.\n702: \t\t// Note: users are recommended to configure the extenders that may return UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n703: \t\t// status ahead of others.\n704: \t\tfeasibleList, failedMap, failedAndUnresolvableMap, err := extender.Filter(pod, feasibleNodes)\n705: \t\tif err != nil {\n706: \t\t\tif extender.IsIgnorable() {\n707: \t\t\t\tlogger.Info(\"Skipping extender as it returned error and has ignorable flag set\", \"extender\", extender, \"err\", err)\n708: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n709: \t\t\t}\n710: \t\t\treturn nil, err\n711: \t\t}\n712: \n713: \t\tfor failedNodeName, failedMsg := range failedAndUnresolvableMap {\n714: \t\t\tvar aggregatedReasons []string\n715: \t\t\tif _, found := statuses[failedNodeName]; found {\n716: \t\t\t\taggregatedReasons = statuses[failedNodeName].Reasons()\n717: \t\t\t}\n718: \t\t\taggregatedReasons = append(aggregatedReasons, failedMsg)\n719: \t\t\tstatuses[failedNodeName] = framework.NewStatus(framework.UnschedulableAndUnresolvable, aggregatedReasons...)\n720: \t\t}\n721: \n722: \t\tfor failedNodeName, failedMsg := range failedMap {\n723: \t\t\tif _, found := failedAndUnresolvableMap[failedNodeName]; found {\n724: \t\t\t\t// failedAndUnresolvableMap takes precedence over failedMap\n725: \t\t\t\t// note that this only happens if the extender returns the node in both maps\n726: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n727: \t\t\t}\n728: \t\t\tif _, found := statuses[failedNodeName]; !found {\n729: \t\t\t\tstatuses[failedNodeName] = framework.NewStatus(framework.Unschedulable, failedMsg)\n730: \t\t\t} else {\n731: \t\t\t\tstatuses[failedNodeName].AppendReason(failedMsg)\n732: \t\t\t}\n733: \t\t}\n734: \n735: \t\tfeasibleNodes = feasibleList\n736: \t}\n737: \treturn feasibleNodes, nil\n738: }\n739: \n740: // prioritizeNodes prioritizes the nodes by running the score plugins,\n741: // which return a score for each node from the call to RunScorePlugins().\n742: // The scores from each plugin are added together to make the score for that node, then\n743: // any extenders are run as well.\n744: // All scores are finally combined (added) to get the total weighted scores of all nodes\n745: func prioritizeNodes(\n746: \tctx context.Context,\n747: \textenders []framework.Extender,\n748: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n749: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n750: \tpod *v1.Pod,\n751: \tnodes []*framework.NodeInfo,\n752: ) ([]framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\n753: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n754: \t// If no priority configs are provided, then all nodes will have a score of one.\n755: \t// This is required to generate the priority list in the required format\n756: \tif len(extenders) == 0 && !fwk.HasScorePlugins() {\n757: \t\tresult := make([]framework.NodePluginScores, 0, len(nodes))\n758: \t\tfor i := range nodes {\n759: \t\t\tresult = append(result, framework.NodePluginScores{\n760: \t\t\t\tName:       nodes[i].Node().Name,\n761: \t\t\t\tTotalScore: 1,\n762: \t\t\t})\n763: \t\t}\n764: \t\treturn result, nil\n765: \t}\n766: \n767: \t// Run PreScore plugins.\n768: \tpreScoreStatus := fwk.RunPreScorePlugins(ctx, state, pod, nodes)\n769: \tif !preScoreStatus.IsSuccess() {\n770: \t\treturn nil, preScoreStatus.AsError()\n771: \t}\n772: \n773: \t// Run the Score plugins.\n774: \tnodesScores, scoreStatus := fwk.RunScorePlugins(ctx, state, pod, nodes)\n775: \tif !scoreStatus.IsSuccess() {\n776: \t\treturn nil, scoreStatus.AsError()\n777: \t}\n778: \n779: \t// Additional details logged at level 10 if enabled.\n780: \tloggerVTen := logger.V(10)\n781: \tif loggerVTen.Enabled() {\n782: \t\tfor _, nodeScore := range nodesScores {\n783: \t\t\tfor _, pluginScore := range nodeScore.Scores {\n784: \t\t\t\tloggerVTen.Info(\"Plugin scored node for pod\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"plugin\", pluginScore.Name, \"node\", nodeScore.Name, \"score\", pluginScore.Score)\n785: \t\t\t}\n786: \t\t}\n787: \t}\n788: \n789: \tif len(extenders) != 0 && nodes != nil {\n790: \t\t// allNodeExtendersScores has all extenders scores for all nodes.\n791: \t\t// It is keyed with node name.\n792: \t\tallNodeExtendersScores := make(map[string]*framework.NodePluginScores, len(nodes))\n793: \t\tvar mu sync.Mutex\n794: \t\tvar wg sync.WaitGroup\n795: \t\tfor i := range extenders {\n796: \t\t\tif !extenders[i].IsInterested(pod) {\n797: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n798: \t\t\t}\n799: \t\t\twg.Add(1)\n800: \t\t\tgo func(extIndex int) {\n801: \t\t\t\tmetrics.Goroutines.WithLabelValues(metrics.PrioritizingExtender).Inc()\n802: \t\t\t\tdefer func() {\n803: \t\t\t\t\tmetrics.Goroutines.WithLabelValues(metrics.PrioritizingExtender).Dec()\n804: \t\t\t\t\twg.Done()\n805: \t\t\t\t}()\n806: \t\t\t\tprioritizedList, weight, err := extenders[extIndex].Prioritize(pod, nodes)\n807: \t\t\t\tif err != nil {\n808: \t\t\t\t\t// Prioritization errors from extender can be ignored, let k8s/other extenders determine the priorities\n809: \t\t\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Failed to run extender's priority function. No score given by this extender.\", \"error\", err, \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"extender\", extenders[extIndex].Name())\n810: \t\t\t\t\treturn\n811: \t\t\t\t}\n812: \t\t\t\tmu.Lock()\n813: \t\t\t\tdefer mu.Unlock()\n814: \t\t\t\tfor i := range *prioritizedList {\n815: \t\t\t\t\tnodename := (*prioritizedList)[i].Host\n816: \t\t\t\t\tscore := (*prioritizedList)[i].Score\n817: \t\t\t\t\tif loggerVTen.Enabled() {\n818: \t\t\t\t\t\tloggerVTen.Info(\"Extender scored node for pod\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"extender\", extenders[extIndex].Name(), \"node\", nodename, \"score\", score)\n819: \t\t\t\t\t}\n820: \n821: \t\t\t\t\t// MaxExtenderPriority may diverge from the max priority used in the scheduler and defined by MaxNodeScore,\n822: \t\t\t\t\t// therefore we need to scale the score returned by extenders to the score range used by the scheduler.\n823: \t\t\t\t\tfinalscore := score * weight * (framework.MaxNodeScore / extenderv1.MaxExtenderPriority)\n824: \n825: \\t\\\"k8s.io/klog/v2\\\"\\n39: \\t\\\"k8s.io/kubernetes/pkg/scheduler/apis/config\\\"\\n40: \\t\\\"k8s.io/kubernetes/pkg/scheduler/framework/parallelize\\\"\\n41: )\\n42: \\n43: // NodeScoreList declares a list of nodes and their scores.\\n44: type NodeScoreList []NodeScore\\n45: \\n46: // NodeScore is a struct with node name and score.\\n47: type NodeScore struct {\\n48: \\tName  string\\n49: \\tScore int64\\n50: }\\n51: \\n52: // NodeToStatusMap declares map from node name to its status.\\n53: type NodeToStatusMap map[string]*Status\\n54: \\n55: // NodePluginScores is a struct with node name and scores for that node.\\n56: type NodePluginScores struct {\\n57: \\t// Name is node name.\\n58: \\tName string\\n59: \\t// Scores is scores from plugins and extenders.\\n60: \\tScores []PluginScore\\n61: \\t// TotalScore is the total score in Scores.\\n62: \\tTotalScore int64\\n63: }\\n64: \\n65: // PluginScore is a struct with plugin/extender name and score.\\n66: type PluginScore struct {\\n67: \\t// Name is the name of plugin or extender.\\n68: \\tName  string\\n69: \\tScore int64\\n70: }\\n71: \\n72: // Code is the Status code/type which is returned from plugins.\\n73: type Code int\\n74: \\n75: // These are predefined codes used in a Status.\\n76: // Note: when you add a new status, you have to add it in `codes` slice below.\\n77: const (\\n78: \\t// Success means that plugin ran correctly and found pod schedulable.\\n79: \\t// NOTE: A nil status is also considered as \\\"Success\\\".\\n80: \\tSuccess Code = iota\\n81: \\t// Error is one of the failures, used for internal plugin errors, unexpected input, etc.\\n82: \\t// Plugin shouldn't return this code for expected failures, like Unschedulable.\\n83: \\t// Since it's the unexpected failure, the scheduling queue registers the pod without unschedulable plugins.\\n84: \\t// Meaning, the Pod will be requeued to activeQ/backoffQ soon.\\n85: \\tError\\n86: \\t// Unschedulable is one of the failures, used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable.\\n87: \\t// If it's returned from PreFilter or Filter, the scheduler might attempt to\\n88: \\t// run other postFilter plugins like preemption to get this pod scheduled.\\n89: \\t// Use UnschedulableAndUnresolvable to make the scheduler skipping other postFilter plugins.\\n90: \\t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\\n91: \\t//\\n92: \\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\\n93: \\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Unschedulable in the last scheduling,\\n94: \\t// the Pod goes through backoff.\\n95: \\tUnschedulable\\n96: \\t// UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable and\\n97: \\t// other postFilter plugins like preemption would not change anything.\\n98: \\t// See the comment on PostFilter interface for more details about how PostFilter should handle this status.\\n99: \\t// Plugins should return Unschedulable if it is possible that the pod can get scheduled\\n100: \\t// after running other postFilter plugins.\\n101: \\t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\\n102: \\t//\\n103: \\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\\n104: \\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable in the last scheduling,\\n105: \\t// the Pod goes through backoff.\\n106: \\tUnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\n107: \\t// Wait is used when a Permit plugin finds a pod scheduling should wait.\\n108: \\tWait\\n109: \\t// Skip is used in the following scenarios:\\n110: \\t// - when a Bind plugin chooses to skip binding.\\n111: \\t// - when a PreFilter plugin returns Skip so that coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped.\\n112: \\t// - when a PreScore plugin returns Skip so that coupled Score plugin will be skipped.\\n113: \\tSkip\\n114: \\t// Pending means that the scheduling process is finished successfully,\\n115: \\t// but the plugin wants to stop the scheduling cycle/binding cycle here.\\n116: \\t//\\n117: \\t// For example, the DRA plugin sometimes needs to wait for the external device driver\\n118: \\t// to provision the resource for the Pod.\\n119: \\t// It's different from when to return Unschedulable/UnschedulableAndUnresolvable,\\n120: \\t// because in this case, the scheduler decides where the Pod can go successfully,\\n121: \\t// but we need to wait for the external component to do something based on that scheduling result.\\n122: \\t//\\n123: \\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\\n124: \\t// In the case of returning Pending, we cannot say the scheduling cycle is wasted\\n125: \\t// because the scheduling result is used to proceed the Pod's scheduling forward,\\n126: \\t// that particular scheduling cycle is failed though.\\n127: \\t// So, Pods rejected by such reasons don't need to suffer a penalty (backoff).\\n128: \\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Pending in the last scheduling,\\n129: \\t// the Pod goes to activeQ directly ignoring backoff.\\n130: \\tPending\\n131: )\\n132: \\n133: // This list should be exactly the same as the codes iota defined above in the same order.\\n134: var codes = []string{\\\"Success\\\", \\\"Error\\\", \\\"Unschedulable\\\", \\\"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\\", \\\"Wait\\\", \\\"Skip\\\", \\\"Pending\\\"}\\n135: \\n136: func (c Code) String() string {\\n137: \\treturn codes[c]\\n138: }\\n139: \\n140: const (\\n141: \\t// MaxNodeScore is the maximum score a Score plugin is expected to return.\\n142: \\tMaxNodeScore int64 = 100\\n143: \\n144: \\t// MinNodeScore is the minimum score a Score plugin is expected to return.\\n145: \\tMinNodeScore int64 = 0\\n146: \\n147: \\t// MaxTotalScore is the maximum total score.\\n148: \\tMaxTotalScore int64 = math.MaxInt64\\n149: )\\n150: \\n151: // PodsToActivateKey is a reserved state key for stashing pods.\\n152: // If the stashed pods are present in unschedulablePods or backoffQ，they will be\\n153: // activated (i.e., moved to activeQ) in two phases:\\n154: // - end of a scheduling cycle if it succeeds (will be cleared from `PodsToActivate` if activated)\\n155: // - end of a binding cycle if it succeeds\\n156: var PodsToActivateKey StateKey = \\\"kubernetes.io/pods-to-activate\\\"\\n157: \\n158: // PodsToActivate stores pods to be activated.\\n159: type PodsToActivate struct {\\n160: \\tsync.Mutex\\n161: \\t// Map is keyed with namespaced pod name, and valued with the pod.\\n162: \\tMap map[string]*v1.Pod\\n163: }\\n164: \\n165: // Clone just returns the same state.\\n166: func (s *PodsToActivate) Clone() StateData {\\n167: \\treturn s\\n168: }\\n169: \\n170: // NewPodsToActivate instantiates a PodsToActivate object.\\n171: func NewPodsToActivate() *PodsToActivate {\\n172: \\treturn &PodsToActivate{Map: make(map[string]*v1.Pod)}\\n173: }\\n174: \\n175: // Status indicates the result of running a plugin. It consists of a code, a\\n176: // message, (optionally) an error, and a plugin name it fails by.\\n177: // When the status code is not Success, the reasons should explain why.\\n178: // And, when code is Success, all the other fields should be empty.\\n179: // NOTE: A nil Status is also considered as Success.\\n180: type Status struct {\\n181: \\tcode    Code\\n182: \\treasons []string\\n183: \\terr     error\\n184: \\t// plugin is an optional field that records the plugin name causes this status.\\n185: \\t// It's set by the framework when code is Unschedulable, UnschedulableAndUnresolvable or Pending.\\n186: \\tplugin string\\n187: }\\n188: \\n189: func (s *Status) WithError(err error) *Status {\\n190: \\ts.err = err\\n191: \\treturn s\\n192: }\\n193: \\n194: // Code returns code of the Status.\\n195: func (s *Status) Code() Code {\\n196: \\tif s == nil {\\n197: \\t\\treturn Success\\n198: \\t}\\n199: \\treturn s.code\\n200: }\\n201: \\n202: // Message returns a concatenated message on reasons of the Status.\\n203: func (s *Status) Message() string {\\n204: \\tif s == nil {\\n205: \\t\\treturn \\\"\\\"\\n206: \\t}\\n207: \\treturn strings.Join(s.Reasons(), \\\", \\\")\\n208: }\\n209: \\n210: // SetPlugin sets the given plugin name to s.plugin.\\n211: func (s *Status) SetPlugin(plugin string) {\\n212: \\ts.plugin = plugin\\n213: }\\n214: \\n215: // WithPlugin sets the given plugin name to s.plugin,\\n216: // and returns the given status object.\\n217: func (s *Status) WithPlugin(plugin string) *Status {\\n218: \\ts.SetPlugin(plugin)\\n219: \\treturn s\\n220: }\\n221: \\n222: // Plugin returns the plugin name which caused this status.\\n223: func (s *Status) Plugin() string {\\n224: \\treturn s.plugin\\n225: }\\n226: \\n227: // Reasons returns reasons of the Status.\\n228: func (s *Status) Reasons() []string {\\n229: \\tif s.err != nil {\\n230: \\t\\treturn append([]string{s.err.Error()}, s.reasons...)\\n231: \\t}\\n232: \\treturn s.reasons\\n233: }\\n234: \\n235: // AppendReason appends given reason to the Status.\\n236: func (s *Status) AppendReason(reason string) {\\n237: \\ts.reasons = append(s.reasons, reason)\\n238: }\\n239: \\n240: // IsSuccess returns true if and only if \\\"Status\\\" is nil or Code is \\\"Success\\\".\\n241: func (s *Status) IsSuccess() bool {\\n242: \\treturn s.Code() == Success\\n243: }\\n244: \\n245: // IsWait returns true if and only if \\\"Status\\\" is non-nil and its Code is \\\"Wait\\\".\\n246: func (s *Status) IsWait() bool {\\n247: \\treturn s.Code() == Wait\\n248: }\\n249: \\n250: // IsSkip returns true if and only if \\\"Status\\\" is non-nil and its Code is \\\"Skip\\\".\\n251: func (s *Status) IsSkip() bool {\\n252: \\treturn s.Code() == Skip\\n253: }\\n254: \\n255: // IsRejected returns true if \\\"Status\\\" is Unschedulable (Unschedulable, UnschedulableAndUnresolvable, or Pending).\\n256: func (s *Status) IsRejected() bool {\\n257: \\tcode := s.Code()\\n258: \\treturn code == Unschedulable || code == UnschedulableAndUnresolvable || code == Pending\\n259: }\\n260: \\n261: // AsError returns nil if the status is a success, a wait or a skip; otherwise returns an \\\"error\\\" object\\n262: // with a concatenated message on reasons of the Status.\\n263: func (s *Status) AsError() error {\\n264: \\tif s.IsSuccess() || s.IsWait() || s.IsSkip() {\\n265: \\t\\treturn nil\\n266: \\t}\\n267: \\tif s.err != nil {\\n268: \\t\\treturn s.err\\n269: \\t}\\n270: \\treturn errors.New(s.Message())\\n271: Each event has a callback function that\\n373: \\t// filters out events to reduce useless retry of Pod's scheduling.\\n374: \\t// The events will be registered when instantiating the internal scheduling queue,\\n375: \\t// and leveraged to build event handlers dynamically.\\n376: \\t// Note: the returned list needs to be static (not depend on configuration parameters);\\n377: \\t// otherwise it would lead to undefined behavior.\\n378: \\t//\\n379: \\t// Appropriate implementation of this function will make Pod's re-scheduling accurate and performant.\\n380: \\tEventsToRegister() []ClusterEventWithHint\\n381: }\\n382: \\n383: // PreFilterExtensions is an interface that is included in plugins that allow specifying\\n384: // callbacks to make incremental updates to its supposedly pre-calculated\\n385: // state.\\n386: type PreFilterExtensions interface {\\n387: \\t// AddPod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\\n388: \\t// of adding podToAdd to the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\\n389: \\tAddPod(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToAdd *PodInfo, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\\n390: \\t// RemovePod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\\n391: \\t// of removing podToRemove from the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\\n392: \\tRemovePod(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToRemove *PodInfo, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\\n393: }\\n394: \\n395: // PreFilterPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \\\"PreFilter\\\" plugins.\\n396: // These plugins are called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle.\\n397: type PreFilterPlugin interface {\\n398: \\tPlugin\\n399: \\t// PreFilter is called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle. All PreFilter\\n400: \\t// plugins must return success or the pod will be rejected. PreFilter could optionally\\n401: \\t// return a PreFilterResult to influence which nodes to evaluate downstream. This is useful\\n402: \\t// for cases where it is possible to determine the subset of nodes to process in O(1) time.\\n403: \\t// When PreFilterResult filters out some Nodes, the framework considers Nodes that are filtered out as getting \\\"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\\".\\n404: \\t// i.e., those Nodes will be out of the candidates of the preemption.\\n405: \\t//\\n406: \\t// When it returns Skip status, returned PreFilterResult and other fields in status are just ignored,\\n407: \\t// and coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\\n408: \\tPreFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod) (*PreFilterResult, *Status)\\n409: \\t// PreFilterExtensions returns a PreFilterExtensions interface if the plugin implements one,\\n410: \\t// or nil if it does not. If Filter doesn't return \\\"Success\\\",\\n430: \\t// it will return \\\"Unschedulable\\\", \\\"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\\" or \\\"Error\\\".\\n431: \\t// For the node being evaluated, Filter plugins should look at the passed\\n432: \\t// nodeInfo reference for this particular node's information (e.g., pods\\n433: \\t// considered to be running on the node) instead of looking it up in the\\n434: \\t// NodeInfoSnapshot because we don't guarantee that they will be the same.\\n435: \\t// For example, during preemption, we may pass a copy of the original\\n436: \\t// nodeInfo object that has some pods removed from it to evaluate the\\n437: \\t// possibility of preempting them to schedule the target pod.\\n438: \\tFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\\n439: }\\n440: \\n441: // PostFilterPlugin is an interface for \\\"PostFilter\\\" plugins. Each event has a callback function that\\n373: \\t// filters out events to reduce useless retry of Pod's scheduling.\\n374: \\t// The events will be registered when instantiating the internal scheduling queue,\\n375: \\t// and leveraged to build event handlers dynamically.\\n376: \\t// Note: the returned list needs to be static (not depend on configuration parameters);\\n377: \\t// otherwise it would lead to undefined behavior.\\n378: \\t//\\n379: \\t// Appropriate implementation of this function will make Pod's re-scheduling accurate and performant.\\n380: \\tEventsToRegister() []ClusterEventWithHint\\n381: }\\n382: \\n383: // PreFilterExtensions is an interface that is included in plugins that allow specifying\\n384: // callbacks to make incremental updates to its supposedly pre-calculated\\n385: // state.\\n386: type PreFilterExtensions interface {\\n387: \\t// AddPod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\\n388: \\t// of adding podToAdd to the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\\n389: \\tAddPod(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToAdd *PodInfo, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\\n390: \\t// RemovePod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\\n391: \\t// of removing podToRemove from the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\\n392: \\tRemovePod(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToRemove *PodInfo, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\\n393: }\\n394: \\n395: // PreFilterPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \\\"PreFilter\\\" plugins.\\n396: // These plugins are called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle.\\n397: type PreFilterPlugin interface {\\n398: \\tPlugin\\n399: \\t// PreFilter is called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle. All PreFilter\\n400: \\t// plugins must return success or the pod will be rejected. PreFilter could optionally\\n401: \\t// return a PreFilterResult to influence which nodes to evaluate downstream. This is useful\\n402: \\t// for cases where it is possible to determine the subset of nodes to process in O(1) time.\\n403: \\t// When PreFilterResult filters out some Nodes, the framework considers Nodes that are filtered out as getting \\\"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\\".\\n404: \\t// i.e., those Nodes will be out of the candidates of the preemption.\\n405: \\t//\\n406: \\t// When it returns Skip status, returned PreFilterResult and other fields in status are just ignored,\\n407: \\t// and coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\\n408: \\tPreFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod) (*PreFilterResult, *Status)\\n409: \\t// PreFilterExtensions returns a PreFilterExtensions interface if the plugin implements one,\\n410: \\t// or nil if it does not. If Filter doesn't return \\\"Success\\\",\\n430: \\t// it will return \\\"Unschedulable\\\", \\\"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\\" or \\\"Error\\\".\\n431: \\t// For the node being evaluated, Filter plugins should look at the passed\\n432: \\t// nodeInfo reference for this particular node's information (e.g., pods\\n433: \\t// considered to be running on the node) instead of looking it up in the\\n434: \\t// NodeInfoSnapshot because we don't guarantee that they will be the same.\\n435: \\t// For example, during preemption, we may pass a copy of the original\\n436: \\t// nodeInfo object that has some pods removed from it to evaluate the\\n437: \\t// possibility of preempting them to schedule the target pod.\\n438: \\tFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\\n439: }\\n440: \\n441: // PostFilterPlugin is an interface for \\\"PostFilter\\\" plugins. func(podInfo1, podInfo2 *QueuedPodInfo) bool\n347: \n348: // QueueSortPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"QueueSort\" plugins.\n349: // These plugins are used to sort pods in the scheduling queue. Only one queue sort\n350: // plugin may be enabled at a time.\n351: type QueueSortPlugin interface {\n352: \tPlugin\n353: \t// Less are used to sort pods in the scheduling queue.\n354: \tLess(*QueuedPodInfo, *QueuedPodInfo) bool\n355: }\n356: \n357: // EnqueueExtensions is an optional interface that plugins can implement to efficiently\n358: // move unschedulable Pods in internal scheduling queues.\n359: // In the scheduler, Pods can be unschedulable by PreEnqueue, PreFilter, Filter, Reserve, and Permit plugins,\n360: // and Pods rejected by these plugins are requeued based on this extension point.\n361: // Failures from other extension points are regarded as temporal errors (e.g., network failure),\n362: // and the scheduler requeue Pods without this extension point - always requeue Pods to activeQ after backoff.\n363: // This is because such temporal errors cannot be resolved by specific cluster events,\n364: // and we have no choise but keep retrying scheduling until the failure is resolved.\n365: //\n366: // Plugins that make pod unschedulable (PreEnqueue, PreFilter, Filter, Reserve, and Permit plugins) should implement this interface,\n367: // otherwise the default implementation will be used, which is less efficient in requeueing Pods rejected by the plugin.\n368: // And, if plugins other than above extension points support this interface, they are just ignored.\n369: type EnqueueExtensions interface {\n370: \tPlugin\n371: \t// EventsToRegister returns a series of possible events that may cause a Pod\n372: \t// failed by this plugin schedulable. Each event has a callback function that\n373: \t// filters out events to reduce useless retry of Pod's scheduling.\n374: \t// The events will be registered when instantiating the internal scheduling queue,\n375: \t// and leveraged to build event handlers dynamically.\n376: \t// Note: the returned list needs to be static (not depend on configuration parameters);\n377: \t// otherwise it would lead to undefined behavior.\n378: \t//\n379: \t// Appropriate implementation of this function will make Pod's re-scheduling accurate and performant.\n380: \tEventsToRegister() []ClusterEventWithHint\n381: }\n382: \n383: // PreFilterExtensions is an interface that is included in plugins that allow specifying\n384: // callbacks to make incremental updates to its supposedly pre-calculated\n385: // state.\n386: type PreFilterExtensions interface {\n387: \t// AddPod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\n388: \t// of adding podToAdd to the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\n389: \tAddPod(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToAdd *PodInfo, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\n390: \t// RemovePod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\n391: \t// of removing podToRemove from the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\n392: \tRemovePod(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToRemove *PodInfo, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\n393: }\n394: \n395: // PreFilterPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PreFilter\" plugins.\n396: // These plugins are called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle.\n397: type PreFilterPlugin interface {\n398: \tPlugin\n399: \t// PreFilter is called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle. All PreFilter\n400: \t// plugins must return success or the pod will be rejected. PreFilter could optionally\n401: \t// return a PreFilterResult to influence which nodes to evaluate downstream. This is useful\n402: \t// for cases where it is possible to determine the subset of nodes to process in O(1) time.\n403: \t// When PreFilterResult filters out some Nodes, the framework considers Nodes that are filtered out as getting \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\".\n404: \t// i.e., those Nodes will be out of the candidates of the preemption.\n405: \t//\n406: \t// When it returns Skip status, returned PreFilterResult and other fields in status are just ignored,\n407: \t// and coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\n408: \tPreFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod) (*PreFilterResult, *Status)\n409: \t// PreFilterExtensions returns a PreFilterExtensions interface if the plugin implements one,\n410: \t// or nil if it does not. A Pre-filter plugin can provide extensions to incrementally\n411: \t// modify its pre-processed info. The framework guarantees that the extensions\n412: \t// AddPod/RemovePod will only be called after PreFilter, possibly on a cloned\n413: \t// CycleState, and may call those functions more than once before calling\n414: \t// Filter again on a specific node.\n415: \tPreFilterExtensions() PreFilterExtensions\n416: }\n417: \n418: // FilterPlugin is an interface for Filter plugins. These plugins are called at the\n419: // filter extension point for filtering out hosts that cannot run a pod.\n420: // This concept used to be called 'predicate' in the original scheduler.\n421: // These plugins should return \"Success\", \"Unschedulable\" or \"Error\" in Status.code.\n422: // However, the scheduler accepts other valid codes as well.\n423: // Anything other than \"Success\" will lead to exclusion of the given host from\n424: // running the pod.\n425: type FilterPlugin interface {\n426: \tPlugin\n427: \t// Filter is called by the scheduling framework.\n428: \t// All FilterPlugins should return \"Success\" to declare that\n429: \t// the given node fits the pod. If Filter doesn't return \"Success\",\n430: \t// it will return \"Unschedulable\", \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\" or \"Error\".\n431: \t// For the node being evaluated, Filter plugins should look at the passed\n432: \t// nodeInfo reference for this particular node's information (e.g., pods\n433: \t// considered to be running on the node) instead of looking it up in the\n434: \t// NodeInfoSnapshot because we don't guarantee that they will be the same.\n435: \t// For example, during preemption, we may pass a copy of the original\n436: \t// nodeInfo object that has some pods removed from it to evaluate the\n437: \t// possibility of preempting them to schedule the target pod.\n438: \tFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\n439: }\n440: \n441: // PostFilterPlugin is an interface for \"PostFilter\" plugins. These plugins are called\n442: // after a pod cannot be scheduled.\n443: type PostFilterPlugin interface {\n444: \tPlugin\n445: \t// PostFilter is called by the scheduling framework\n446: \t// when the scheduling cycle failed at PreFilter or Filter by Unschedulable or UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n447: \t// NodeToStatusMap has statuses that each Node got in the Filter phase.\n448: \t// If this scheduling cycle failed at PreFilter, all Nodes have the status from the rejector PreFilter plugin in NodeToStatusMap.\n449: \t// Note that the scheduling framework runs PostFilter plugins even when PreFilter returned UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n450: \t// In that case, NodeToStatusMap contains all Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n451: \t//\n452: \t// Also, ignoring Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is the responsibility of each PostFilter plugin,\n453: \t// meaning NodeToStatusMap obviously could have Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n454: \t// and the scheduling framework does call PostFilter even when all Nodes in NodeToStatusMap are UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n455: \t//\n456: \t// A PostFilter plugin should return one of the following statuses:\n457: \t// - Unschedulable: the plugin gets executed successfully but the pod cannot be made schedulable.\n458: \t// - Success: the plugin gets executed successfully and the pod can be made schedulable.\n459: \t// - Error: the plugin aborts due to some internal error.\n460: \t//\n461: \t// Informational plugins should be configured ahead of other ones, and always return Unschedulable status.\n462: \t// Optionally, a non-nil PostFilterResult may be returned along with a Success status. For example,\n463: \t// a preemption plugin may choose to return nominatedNodeName, so that framework can reuse that to update the\n464: \t// preemptor pod's .spec.status.nominatedNodeName field.\n465: \tPostFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, filteredNodeStatusMap NodeToStatusMap) (*PostFilterResult, *Status)\n466: }\n467: \n468: // PreScorePlugin is an interface for \"PreScore\" plugin. PreScore is an\n469: // informational extension point. Plugins will be called with a list of nodes\n470: // that passed the filtering phase. A plugin may use this data to update internal\n471: // state or to generate logs/metrics.\n472: type PreScorePlugin interface {\n473: \tPlugin\n474: \t// PreScore is called by the scheduling framework after a list of nodes\n475: \t// passed the filtering phase. All prescore plugins must return success or\n476: \t// the pod will be rejected\n477: \t// When it returns Skip status, other fields in status are just ignored,\n478: \t// and coupled Score plugin will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\n479: \tPreScore(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodes []*NodeInfo) *Status\n480: }\n481: \n482: // ScoreExtensions is an interface for Score extended functionality.\n483: type ScoreExtensions interface {\n484: \t// NormalizeScore is called for all node scores produced by the same plugin's \"Score\"\n485: \t// method. It must return success and an integer\n495: \t// indicating the rank of the node. These plugins should\n506: // return only Success or Error in Status.code. However, the scheduler accepts\n507: // other valid codes as well. Anything other than Success will lead to\n508: // rejection of the pod.\n509: type ReservePlugin interface {\n510: \tPlugin\n511: \t// Reserve is called by the scheduling framework when the scheduler cache is\n512: \t// updated. the sched.nextStartNodeIndex regardless of whether an error has occurred\n500: \t// this is helpful to make sure that all the nodes have a chance to be searched\n501: \tprocessedNodes := {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01YD63mLVb4LG37kPtLZTGrU","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_011sAhmyWAKkfLNBhzCkp5c4","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/solution.md","content":"# Kubernetes Scheduler Architecture Analysis\n\n## Overview\n\nThe Kubernetes scheduler is responsible for assigning unscheduled Pods to Nodes. It follows a two-phase design: a **scheduling cycle** that evaluates and selects a node, and a **binding cycle** that commits the pod assignment. The scheduler uses an extensible **plugin framework** that allows both in-tree and out-of-tree plugins to participate in scheduling decisions at well-defined extension points.\n\n---\n\n## Files Examined\n\n### Core Scheduler Files\n- **pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go** — Main `Scheduler` struct containing queue, cache, framework profiles, and initialization logic; implements `New()` and `Run()` entry points\n- **pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go** — Main scheduling loop (`ScheduleOne()`) and orchestration of scheduling/binding cycles (`schedulingCycle()`, `bindingCycle()`)\n\n### Framework & Plugin Infrastructure\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/interface.go** — Defines all plugin interfaces (PreEnqueue, QueueSort, PreFilter, Filter, PostFilter, PreScore, Score, Reserve, Permit, PreBind, Bind, PostBind), `Framework`, `Handle`, and `Status` types\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/cycle_state.go** — `CycleState` struct for plugin state management across a scheduling cycle using thread-safe storage\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go** — `frameworkImpl` implementing the `Framework` interface; manages plugin registration and execution\n\n### Scheduling Queue & Cache\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/queue/scheduling_queue.go** — `PriorityQueue` implementation with three sub-queues: activeQ, backoffQ, unschedulablePods\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/cache.go** — `cacheImpl` maintaining node information, tracking assumed pods, and managing cache assumptions\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/node_tree.go** — Tree structure for efficient node lookup\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/snapshot.go** — Immutable snapshot of cache taken at scheduling cycle start\n\n### Event Handling & Extenders\n- **pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go** — Event handlers for pod/node/storage class updates triggering queue requeuing\n- **pkg/scheduler/extender.go** — HTTP-based external scheduler extender interface\n\n---\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n### 1. **Entry Point: Scheduler Initialization & Run**\n   - **`scheduler.New(ctx, client, informerFactory, ...)`** (pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go:253)\n     - Creates in-tree plugin registry\n     - Builds scheduler profiles and framework instances\n     - Initializes scheduling queue (PriorityQueue)\n     - Initializes scheduler cache\n     - Registers event handlers for pods/nodes\n     - Returns `*Scheduler` instance\n\n   - **`sched.Run(ctx)`** (pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go:435)\n     - Starts scheduling queue goroutines\n     - Launches main scheduling loop via `wait.UntilWithContext(ctx, sched.ScheduleOne, 0)`\n\n### 2. **Main Scheduling Loop**\n   - **`sched.ScheduleOne(ctx)`** (pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:66)\n     - Calls `sched.NextPod(logger)` → pops from `SchedulingQueue`\n     - Retrieves framework for pod's scheduler name\n     - Calls **`sched.schedulingCycle(ctx, state, fwk, podInfo, start, podsToActivate)`** (line 111)\n     - On success, launches binding cycle in goroutine\n\n### 3. **Scheduling Cycle (Pod Selection)**\n   - **`schedulingCycle()`** (pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:139)\n     1. Calls **`sched.SchedulePod(ctx, fwk, state, pod)`** → **`sched.schedulePod()`** (line 390)\n        - Updates cache snapshot via `sched.Cache.UpdateSnapshot()`\n        - **Phase A: Filtering**\n          - Calls `sched.findNodesThatFitPod(ctx, fwk, state, pod)`\n          - Runs **PreFilter plugins** via `fwk.RunPreFilterPlugins()` (line 453)\n          - Calls **`findNodesThatPassFilters()`** (line 573)\n            - Runs **Filter plugins** in parallel via `fwk.Parallelizer().Until()` (line 640)\n            - Calls `fwk.RunFilterPluginsWithNominatedPods(ctx, state, pod, nodeInfo)` per node\n          - Processes extender filters via `findNodesThatPassExtenders()`\n        - **Phase B: Scoring**\n          - Calls **`prioritizeNodes()`** (line 425)\n          - Runs **PreScore plugins** via `fwk.RunPreScorePlugins()`\n          - Runs **Score plugins** on each feasible node via `fwk.RunScorePlugins()`\n          - Scores with extenders (if present)\n        - **Phase C: Selection**\n          - Calls `selectHost()` to pick best-scored node\n\n     2. On success, **assumes pod** via `sched.assume(logger, assumedPod, nodeName)` (line 198)\n        - Adds pod to cache with assumed state\n\n     3. Runs **Reserve plugins** via `fwk.RunReservePluginsReserve()` (line 209)\n        - If fails, calls `fwk.RunReservePluginsUnreserve()` and `sched.Cache.ForgetPod()`\n\n     4. Runs **Permit plugins** via `fwk.RunPermitPlugins()` (line 231)\n        - Creates waiting pods if any plugin returns \"Wait\"\n\n### 4. **Binding Cycle (Pod Commitment)**\n   - **`bindingCycle()`** (pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:265)\n     1. Waits on **Permit plugins** via `fwk.WaitOnPermit()` (line 278)\n\n     2. Runs **PreBind plugins** via `fwk.RunPreBindPlugins()` (line 294)\n        - Performs pre-binding validation (e.g., PVC checks)\n\n     3. Runs **Bind plugins** via `sched.bind()` (line 299)\n        - Default: calls API server to create Pod binding\n        - Can be overridden by custom bind plugins\n\n     4. Runs **PostBind plugins** via `fwk.RunPostBindPlugins()` (line 312)\n        - Informational, performs cleanup/logging\n\n---\n\n## Architecture Analysis\n\n### Design Patterns\n\n#### 1. **Plugin Framework Architecture**\nThe scheduler uses an **extension point** pattern where plugins implement specific interfaces and hook into well-defined points in the scheduling pipeline:\n\n```\nExtension Points (in execution order):\n├─ PreEnqueue (before pod enters activeQ)\n├─ QueueSort (sorts pods in queue)\n├─ PreFilter (pod-level filtering setup, can filter out nodes)\n├─ Filter (per-node filtering, parallel execution)\n├─ PostFilter (preemption/recovery if no nodes fit)\n├─ PreScore (informational, after filtering)\n├─ Score (per-node scoring, parallel execution)\n├─ Reserve (mark node as having resources reserved)\n├─ Permit (final gate before binding, can wait)\n├─ PreBind (validation before binding)\n├─ Bind (performs actual binding)\n└─ PostBind (post-binding cleanup)\n```\n\n#### 2. **Two-Phase Scheduling Design**\n- **Scheduling Cycle** (synchronous): Evaluates pods/nodes, makes scheduling decision\n- **Binding Cycle** (asynchronous): Commits binding to API server without blocking other scheduling\n\nThis enables the scheduler to continue scheduling other pods while binding happens asynchronously.\n\n#### 3. **State Isolation via CycleState**\nEach scheduling cycle creates a fresh `CycleState` that plugins use to store temporary data:\n- Thread-safe storage using `sync.Map`\n- Plugins write computed state in PreFilter/PreScore\n- Other plugins read this state in Filter/Score\n- Allows plugins to share information without direct coupling\n\n#### 4. **Assume-Release Pattern**\nBefore binding completes, the pod is \"assumed\" in the cache:\n- Updates cache immediately after successful Reserve phase\n- Allows next scheduling cycle to see \"reserved\" resources\n- If binding fails later, cache is updated via `ForgetPod()`\n- Prevents scheduling multiple pods to same space\n\n#### 5. **Queue-based Requeuing**\nPods move through queue states based on scheduling outcome:\n```\nPod States in Queue:\n├─ activeQ: Ready to be scheduled\n├─ backoffQ: Unschedulable but will retry after backoff\n└─ unschedulablePods: Unschedulable, stays until cluster event triggers requeue\n```\n\n#### 6. **Snapshot Isolation**\nCache snapshot taken at cycle start ensures consistent view throughout filtering/scoring:\n- Prevents race conditions between cycle phases\n- Snapshot remains unchanged during Permit phase\n- Binding cycle may see different cluster state (acceptable)\n\n### Component Responsibilities\n\n#### **Scheduler (pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go)**\n- Orchestrates overall scheduling workflow\n- Maintains cache and queue\n- Manages framework profiles (supports multiple scheduler instances)\n- Registers event handlers to respond to cluster changes\n\n#### **Framework (pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go)**\n- Loads and initializes plugins\n- Routes scheduling requests through plugin extension points\n- Manages plugin execution (sequential or parallel)\n- Provides Handle interface for plugins to access cluster state\n\n#### **SchedulingQueue (pkg/scheduler/internal/queue/scheduling_queue.go)**\n- Maintains pod queues with priority\n- Moves pods between queues based on scheduling outcomes\n- Integrates with plugins for event-driven requeuing\n- Supports backoff for failed pods\n\n#### **Cache (pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/cache.go)**\n- Maintains node information (CPU, memory, pods)\n- Tracks assumed pods with configurable TTL\n- Provides snapshots for consistent scheduling cycles\n- Expires long-lived assumptions automatically\n\n#### **Plugins (via plugin interfaces in framework/interface.go)**\n- **PreFilter/Filter**: Determine node feasibility\n- **Score**: Rank feasible nodes\n- **Reserve/Permit**: Gate decisions before binding\n- **Bind/PreBind/PostBind**: Manage binding lifecycle\n- **PostFilter**: Implement preemption or recovery logic\n\n### Data Flow\n\n#### **Scheduling Cycle Data Flow**\n```\nPod from Queue\n    ↓\n[CycleState created]\n    ↓\n[Cache Snapshot taken]\n    ↓\nRunPreFilterPlugins() ← Plugins can exclude entire node sets\n    ↓\nRunFilterPlugins() on each node (parallel) ← Per-node feasibility\n    ↓\n[Feasible nodes list]\n    ↓\nRunPreScorePlugins() ← Informational, prepare scoring state\n    ↓\nRunScorePlugins() on feasible nodes (parallel) ← Rank nodes\n    ↓\nselectHost() ← Pick highest-scored node\n    ↓\nCache.AssumedPodAdded() ← Reserve resources in cache\n    ↓\nRunReservePlugins() ← Plugins update internal state\n    ↓\nRunPermitPlugins() ← Final gate (can wait)\n    ↓\nReturn: Success → Launch Binding Cycle\n```\n\n#### **Binding Cycle Data Flow**\n```\n[From Scheduling Cycle: Assumed Pod Info]\n    ↓\nWaitOnPermit() ← Block if Permit returned \"Wait\"\n    ↓\nRunPreBindPlugins() ← Validation (e.g., PVC checks)\n    ↓\nRunBindPlugins() ← Commit to API server\n    ↓\nRunPostBindPlugins() ← Cleanup/logging\n    ↓\nQueue.Done() ← Mark pod processing complete\n    ↓\nSuccess: Pod bound to node\n```\n\n### Interface Contracts\n\n#### **Plugin Interface (framework/interface.go:329)**\nAll plugins must implement:\n```go\ntype Plugin interface {\n    Name() string\n}\n```\n\n#### **Extension Point Interfaces**\n- **PreFilterPlugin** → `PreFilter(ctx, state, pod) (*PreFilterResult, *Status)`\n- **FilterPlugin** → `Filter(ctx, state, pod, nodeInfo) *Status`\n- **ScorePlugin** → `Score(ctx, state, pod, nodeName) (int64, *Status)`\n- **ReservePlugin** → `Reserve(ctx, state, pod, nodeName) *Status`\n- **PermitPlugin** → `Permit(ctx, state, pod, nodeName) (*Status, time.Duration)`\n- **BindPlugin** → `Bind(ctx, state, pod, nodeName) *Status`\n\n#### **Status Codes**\n- `Success` (nil): Operation succeeded\n- `Unschedulable`: Pod doesn't fit (might succeed after preemption)\n- `UnschedulableAndUnresolvable`: Pod doesn't fit (preemption won't help)\n- `Wait`: Permit plugin wants to wait before binding\n- `Error`: Unexpected failure\n- `Pending`: Scheduling succeeded but waiting for external action\n\n#### **Framework Handle Interface (framework/interface.go:663)**\nPlugins receive `Handle` providing:\n- `SnapshotSharedLister()` → Access to node/pod cache snapshots\n- `ClientSet()` → Kubernetes client\n- `EventRecorder()` → Record events\n- Waiting pod management\n- Pod nominator for preemption hints\n\n### Queue Integration\n\n#### **Scheduling Queue States**\n- **activeQ**: Heap of pods ready to schedule, sorted by priority\n- **backoffQ**: Pods that failed and are backing off\n- **unschedulablePods**: Pods that can't be scheduled now\n\n#### **Pod Movement Triggers**\n- Pod creation/update → added to activeQ\n- Pod rejected unschedulable → moved to backoffQ\n- Long unschedulable pod → expires from unschedulablePods to activeQ\n- Cluster event (node added, resource freed) → pods requeued via `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()`\n\n#### **Queueing Hints (plugin EnqueueExtensions)**\nPlugins can register `EventsToRegister()` to specify which cluster events should requeue pods they rejected:\n- Avoids unnecessary requeuing\n- Improves scheduling efficiency\n- Plugins return QueueingHint for events they care about\n\n### Error Handling & Recovery\n\n#### **Scheduling Cycle Failures**\n1. **PreFilter failure** → Mark all nodes unschedulable, trigger PostFilter\n2. **Filter/Score failure** → Continue with other nodes or fall through\n3. **PostFilter (preemption)** → Attempts to preempt pods to make room\n4. **Reserve failure** → Calls `Unreserve()` on all plugins, forgets pod\n\n#### **Binding Cycle Failures**\n1. **PreBind/Bind failure** → Trigger `Unreserve()`, forget pod from cache\n2. **Assumed pod expires** → Cache automatically forgets after TTL\n3. **Pod update during cycle** → Binding cycle detects and handles gracefully\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Kubernetes scheduler v1.30.0 implements a sophisticated two-phase scheduling architecture that separates pod selection (scheduling cycle) from commitment (binding cycle). It uses an extensible plugin framework with 12 extension points, enabling both in-tree and out-of-tree plugins to influence decisions without tight coupling. The scheduler maintains a priority-based queue and an intelligent cache that tracks node resources and assumed pod reservations. By using CycleState for isolation, snapshots for consistency, and the assume-release pattern for optimistic concurrency, the scheduler efficiently handles large clusters while allowing asynchronous binding without blocking other scheduling decisions. This design enables high throughput and low latency pod scheduling while maintaining correctness and extensibility.\n\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2024,"cache_read_input_tokens":85599,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2024},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"443fda24-0457-421e-9021-efd911ae493b","uuid":"2ae2ecc2-b4d3-4838-9cd7-dcf4c50fd983"}

It follows a two-phase design: a **scheduling cycle** that evaluates and selects a node, and a **binding cycle** that commits the pod assignment. The scheduler uses an extensible **plugin framework** that allows both in-tree and out-of-tree plugins to participate in scheduling decisions at well-defined extension points.\n\n---\n\n## Files Examined\n\n### Core Scheduler Files\n- **pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go** — Main `Scheduler` struct containing queue, cache, framework profiles, and initialization logic; implements `New()` and `Run()` entry points\n- **pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go** — Main scheduling loop (`ScheduleOne()`) and orchestration of scheduling/binding cycles (`schedulingCycle()`, `bindingCycle()`)\n\n### Framework & Plugin Infrastructure\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/interface.go** — Defines all plugin interfaces (PreEnqueue, QueueSort, PreFilter, Filter, PostFilter, PreScore, Score, Reserve, Permit, PreBind, Bind, PostBind), `Framework`, `Handle`, and `Status` types\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/cycle_state.go** — `CycleState` struct for plugin state management across a scheduling cycle using thread-safe storage\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go** — `frameworkImpl` implementing the `Framework` interface; manages plugin registration and execution\n\n### Scheduling Queue & Cache\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/queue/scheduling_queue.go** — `PriorityQueue` implementation with three sub-queues: activeQ, backoffQ, unschedulablePods\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/cache.go** — `cacheImpl` maintaining node information, tracking assumed pods, and managing cache assumptions\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/node_tree.go** — Tree structure for efficient node lookup\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/snapshot.go** — Immutable snapshot of cache taken at scheduling cycle start\n\n### Event Handling & Extenders\n- **pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go** — Event handlers for pod/node/storage class updates triggering queue requeuing\n- **pkg/scheduler/extender.go** — HTTP-based external scheduler extender interface\n\n---\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n### 1. **Entry Point: Scheduler Initialization & Run**\n   - **`scheduler.New(ctx, client, informerFactory, ...)`** (pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go:253)\n     - Creates in-tree plugin registry\n     - Builds scheduler profiles and framework instances\n     - Initializes scheduling queue (PriorityQueue)\n     - Initializes scheduler cache\n     - Registers event handlers for pods/nodes\n     - Returns `*Scheduler` instance\n\n   - **`sched.Run(ctx)`** (pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go:435)\n     - Starts scheduling queue goroutines\n     - Launches main scheduling loop via `wait.UntilWithContext(ctx, sched.ScheduleOne, 0)`\n\n### 2. **Main Scheduling Loop**\n   - **`sched.ScheduleOne(ctx)`** (pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:66)\n     - Calls `sched.NextPod(logger)` → pops from `SchedulingQueue`\n     - Retrieves framework for pod's scheduler name\n     - Calls **`sched.schedulingCycle(ctx, state, fwk, podInfo, start, podsToActivate)`** (line 111)\n     - On success, launches binding cycle in goroutine\n\n### 3. **Scheduling Cycle (Pod Selection)**\n   - **`schedulingCycle()`** (pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:139)\n     1. Calls **`sched.SchedulePod(ctx, fwk, state, pod)`** → **`sched.schedulePod()`** (line 390)\n        - Updates cache snapshot via `sched.Cache.UpdateSnapshot()`\n        - **Phase A: Filtering**\n          - Calls `sched.findNodesThatFitPod(ctx, fwk, state, pod)`\n          - Runs **PreFilter plugins** via `fwk.RunPreFilterPlugins()` (line 453)\n          - Calls **`findNodesThatPassFilters()`** (line 573)\n            - Runs **Filter plugins** in parallel via `fwk.Parallelizer().Until()` (line 640)\n            - Calls `fwk.RunFilterPluginsWithNominatedPods(ctx, state, pod, nodeInfo)` per node\n          - Processes extender filters via `findNodesThatPassExtenders()`\n        - **Phase B: Scoring**\n          - Calls **`prioritizeNodes()`** (line 425)\n          - Runs **PreScore plugins** via `fwk.RunPreScorePlugins()`\n          - Runs **Score plugins** on each feasible node via `fwk.RunScorePlugins()`\n          - Scores with extenders (if present)\n        - **Phase C: Selection**\n          - Calls `selectHost()` to pick best-scored node\n\n     2. On success, **assumes pod** via `sched.assume(logger, assumedPod, nodeName)` (line 198)\n        - Adds pod to cache with assumed state\n\n     3. Runs **Reserve plugins** via `fwk.RunReservePluginsReserve()` (line 209)\n        - If fails, calls `fwk.RunReservePluginsUnreserve()` and `sched.Cache.ForgetPod()`\n\n     4. Runs **Permit plugins** via `fwk.RunPermitPlugins()` (line 231)\n        - Creates waiting pods if any plugin returns \"Wait\"\n\n### 4. **Binding Cycle (Pod Commitment)**\n   - **`bindingCycle()`** (pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:265)\n     1. Waits on **Permit plugins** via `fwk.WaitOnPermit()` (line 278)\n\n     2. Runs **PreBind plugins** via `fwk.RunPreBindPlugins()` (line 294)\n        - Performs pre-binding validation (e.g., PVC checks)\n\n     3. Runs **Bind plugins** via `sched.bind()` (line 299)\n        - Default: calls API server to create Pod binding\n        - Can be overridden by custom bind plugins\n\n     4. Runs **PostBind plugins** via `fwk.RunPostBindPlugins()` (line 312)\n        - Informational, performs cleanup/logging\n\n---\n\n## Architecture Analysis\n\n### Design Patterns\n\n#### 1. **Plugin Framework Architecture**\nThe scheduler uses an **extension point** pattern where plugins implement specific interfaces and hook into well-defined points in the scheduling pipeline:\n\n```\nExtension Points (in execution order):\n├─ PreEnqueue (before pod enters activeQ)\n├─ QueueSort (sorts pods in queue)\n├─ PreFilter (pod-level filtering setup, can filter out nodes)\n├─ Filter (per-node filtering, parallel execution)\n├─ PostFilter (preemption/recovery if no nodes fit)\n├─ PreScore (informational, after filtering)\n├─ Score (per-node scoring, parallel execution)\n├─ Reserve (mark node as having resources reserved)\n├─ Permit (final gate before binding, can wait)\n├─ PreBind (validation before binding)\n├─ Bind (performs actual binding)\n└─ PostBind (post-binding cleanup)\n```\n\n#### 2. **Two-Phase Scheduling Design**\n- **Scheduling Cycle** (synchronous): Evaluates pods/nodes, makes scheduling decision\n- **Binding Cycle** (asynchronous): Commits binding to API server without blocking other scheduling\n\nThis enables the scheduler to continue scheduling other pods while binding happens asynchronously.\n\n#### 3. **State Isolation via CycleState**\nEach scheduling cycle creates a fresh `CycleState` that plugins use to store temporary data:\n- Thread-safe storage using `sync.Map`\n- Plugins write computed state in PreFilter/PreScore\n- Other plugins read this state in Filter/Score\n- Allows plugins to share information without direct coupling\n\n#### 4. **Assume-Release Pattern**\nBefore binding completes, the pod is \"assumed\" in the cache:\n- Updates cache immediately after successful Reserve phase\n- Allows next scheduling cycle to see \"reserved\" resources\n- If binding fails later, cache is updated via `ForgetPod()`\n- Prevents scheduling multiple pods to same space\n\n#### 5. **Queue-based Requeuing**\nPods move through queue states based on scheduling outcome:\n```\nPod States in Queue:\n├─ activeQ: Ready to be scheduled\n├─ backoffQ: Unschedulable but will retry after backoff\n└─ unschedulablePods: Unschedulable, stays until cluster event triggers requeue\n```\n\n#### 6. **Snapshot Isolation**\nCache snapshot taken at cycle start ensures consistent view throughout filtering/scoring:\n- Prevents race conditions between cycle phases\n- Snapshot remains unchanged during Permit phase\n- Binding cycle may see different cluster state (acceptable)\n\n### Component Responsibilities\n\n#### **Scheduler (pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go)**\n- Orchestrates overall scheduling workflow\n- Maintains cache and queue\n- Manages framework profiles (supports multiple scheduler instances)\n- Registers event handlers to respond to cluster changes\n\n#### **Framework (pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go)**\n- Loads and initializes plugins\n- Routes scheduling requests through plugin extension points\n- Manages plugin execution (sequential or parallel)\n- Provides Handle interface for plugins to access cluster state\n\n#### **SchedulingQueue (pkg/scheduler/internal/queue/scheduling_queue.go)**\n- Maintains pod queues with priority\n- Moves pods between queues based on scheduling outcomes\n- Integrates with plugins for event-driven requeuing\n- Supports backoff for failed pods\n\n#### **Cache (pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/cache.go)**\n- Maintains node information (CPU, memory, pods)\n- Tracks assumed pods with configurable TTL\n- Provides snapshots for consistent scheduling cycles\n- Expires long-lived assumptions automatically\n\n#### **Plugins (via plugin interfaces in framework/interface.go)**\n- **PreFilter/Filter**: Determine node feasibility\n- **Score**: Rank feasible nodes\n- **Reserve/Permit**: Gate decisions before binding\n- **Bind/PreBind/PostBind**: Manage binding lifecycle\n- **PostFilter**: Implement preemption or recovery logic\n\n### Data Flow\n\n#### **Scheduling Cycle Data Flow**\n```\nPod from Queue\n    ↓\n[CycleState created]\n    ↓\n[Cache Snapshot taken]\n    ↓\nRunPreFilterPlugins() ← Plugins can exclude entire node sets\n    ↓\nRunFilterPlugins() on each node (parallel) ← Per-node feasibility\n    ↓\n[Feasible nodes list]\n    ↓\nRunPreScorePlugins() ← Informational, prepare scoring state\n    ↓\nRunScorePlugins() on feasible nodes (parallel) ← Rank nodes\n    ↓\nselectHost() ← Pick highest-scored node\n    ↓\nCache.AssumedPodAdded() ← Reserve resources in cache\n    ↓\nRunReservePlugins() ← Plugins update internal state\n    ↓\nRunPermitPlugins() ← Final gate (can wait)\n    ↓\nReturn: Success → Launch Binding Cycle\n```\n\n#### **Binding Cycle Data Flow**\n```\n[From Scheduling Cycle: Assumed Pod Info]\n    ↓\nWaitOnPermit() ← Block if Permit returned \"Wait\"\n    ↓\nRunPreBindPlugins() ← Validation (e.g., PVC checks)\n    ↓\nRunBindPlugins() ← Commit to API server\n    ↓\nRunPostBindPlugins() ← Cleanup/logging\n    ↓\nQueue.Done() ← Mark pod processing complete\n    ↓\nSuccess: Pod bound to node\n```\n\n### Interface Contracts\n\n#### **Plugin Interface (framework/interface.go:329)**\nAll plugins must implement:\n```go\ntype Plugin interface {\n    Name() string\n}\n```\n\n#### **Extension Point Interfaces**\n- **PreFilterPlugin** → `PreFilter(ctx, state, pod) (*PreFilterResult, *Status)`\n- **FilterPlugin** → `Filter(ctx, state, pod, nodeInfo) *Status`\n- **ScorePlugin** → `Score(ctx, state, pod, nodeName) (int64, *Status)`\n- **ReservePlugin** → `Reserve(ctx, state, pod, nodeName) *Status`\n- **PermitPlugin** → `Permit(ctx, state, pod, nodeName) (*Status, time.Duration)`\n- **BindPlugin** → `Bind(ctx, state, pod, nodeName) *Status`\n\n#### **Status Codes**\n- `Success` (nil): Operation succeeded\n- `Unschedulable`: Pod doesn't fit (might succeed after preemption)\n- `UnschedulableAndUnresolvable`: Pod doesn't fit (preemption won't help)\n- `Wait`: Permit plugin wants to wait before binding\n- `Error`: Unexpected failure\n- `Pending`: Scheduling succeeded but waiting for external action\n\n#### **Framework Handle Interface (framework/interface.go:663)**\nPlugins receive `Handle` providing:\n- `SnapshotSharedLister()` →
